Yet they do not know that the five metals and eight minerals are substances of form and matter, their kinds disparate and natures distinct. The Golden Elixir arises from nothing to become something—how could the supreme medicine consent to merge and dwell together with them? Thus, all who practice this art meet with a thousand failures for every ten thousand attempts, desiring success yet growing deluded. Why? Because their beginnings lack cause and condition, their measures lose hold of proper discipline.

Hence it is said: the world does not recognize true lead and mercury, taking common cinnabar and quicksilver to be them. Time and again, they waste fire and squander wealth, yet achieve no success, until their hair turns white in bewilderment, and they sigh in vain at emptiness. Alas! The true Dao is simple and unburdensome; its profound words are bland and flavorless. Who would believe and practice them? Even those who receive the correct transmission may, midway, generate doubt, turning from the right path to deviance—such cases abound.

The *Tongxuan Secret Formula* states: “Many rely on cleverness, forcibly asserting right and wrong. Though they hear the essential teachings, they contradict themselves. Thus, they turn from the great Dao and cling to deluded paths, peering at heaven through a tube without broad vision—how can they discuss the boundless mysteries of the future?”

The *Fire Record* is not idly composed; it elucidates through the *Yi*’s principles. The recumbent-moon method employs the crucible: the White Tiger as the pivot of refinement, mercury as the flowing pearl, the Green Dragon dwelling with it. Raising the east to meet the west, hun and po naturally constrain each other. Above, the trigram *dui* holds the number eight; below, *gen* also holds eight. The two eights unite their essence, and the body of *qian* and *kun* is complete—two eights correspond to one catty. The Dao of the *Yi* stands upright, never tilting.

Zhenyi Zi, Peng Xiao, said: “Though there are records of fire, one must abide by the Dao of the *Yi* in practice, following the hexagrams’ lines and circulating through *pi* and *tai*. The crucible of the recumbent moon is the upturned moon. The Metal Tiger within serves as the pivot of the medicine; the Vermilion Mercury and Green Dragon are governed by *bing* and *ding*. The Vermilion Bird pursues and chases in time, all entering the golden womb—hence it is called ‘raising the east to meet the west.’ *Hun* and *po* are the Green Dragon’s *hun* in the east and the White Tiger’s *po* in the west. The upper and lower eights combine to form the number of one catty, completing the forms of *qian* and *kun*, matching the number of one celestial cycle.”

Baoyi Zi, Chen Xianwei, said: “Ancient elixir texts describe the functions of fire timing, calling them *Fire Records*—altogether six hundred chapters. Their precautions do not exceed the *Zhou Yi*. Was the *Fire Record* composed idly, without basis? It should be elucidated through the *Yi*’s principles. The *Yi* has three hundred eighty-four lines, corresponding to the fire timing of the celestial cycle. The upper and lower eights, two eights making one catty, and one catty equaling three hundred eighty-four *zhu*—these precisely match the hexagrams’ lines. The *qian* lines number one hundred ninety-two, and the *kun* lines one hundred ninety-two, thus the Dao of *qian* and *kun* is complete.

The recumbent-moon crucible refers to the body and function of the Mysterious Pass’s single aperture. That aperture is half white, half black, like a half-moon—hence it is called the recumbent-moon crucible. Knowing the recumbent moon as the crucible and furnace, one has grasped more than half of the Great Elixir’s Dao.

The White Tiger below serves as the pivot for kindling fire; the Green Dragon above stirs the winds and waves of rising clouds. Within, true mercury transforms into flowing pearls. Thus, the eastern dragon and western tiger unite, yin *po* and yang *hun* restrain each other, divine workings circulate in the golden crucible, and sacred medicine is forged in the jade furnace. The mechanism of creation is inverted, the functions of *qian* and *kun* are overturned—who but the most profoundly penetrating in the world could achieve this?”

Shangyang Zi, Chen Zhixu, said: “These words speak of the crucible and furnace, the Green Dragon and White Tiger, the *qi* of the eights, the recumbent-moon crucible, the White Tiger, the upper eight, *dui*, and *po*—all pertain to the west. That is the jade pool.”

“Mercury is called ‘flowing pearl,’ the Green Dragon, the lower *kan*, *gen*, and *hun*—all pertain to the east. That is the self, the golden crucible.

The recumbent-moon crucible is none other than the Great Unity’s divine furnace, called the yin crucible. Its recumbent and upturned form resembles the moon at its first crescent. The White Tiger is the being of the western *dui* palace. When heaven and earth first divided, its primordial essence belonged to that quarter. The tiger’s might responds when struck, its refined radiance nurturing the myriad beings. Though it can wound or kill, it harbors the vastness of the Great Vehicle. King Wen, in his profound *Yi*, said: ‘Treading on the tiger’s tail, it does not bite the man—sublime.’ And again: ‘Treading the Way, level and vast, the secluded one’s steadfastness brings good fortune.’ Confucius said: ‘Joyful yet responsive to *qian*,’ and ‘Treading the white path, one walks alone in fulfillment of one’s wish.’

The adept who refines the elixir, knowing to fear this tiger, must first subdue and tame it. Once tamed, it becomes the pivot for refinement and will not bite. *Li* is the sun, mercury; within it lies cinnabar, called ‘flowing pearl.’ The Green Dragon is the being of the eastern *zhen* palace. When the kalpa’s cycle is complete, its primordial essence belongs to the self. The dragon’s might transforms and responds, moving clouds and sending rain, shaping the myriad forms. *Qian*’s nine-two says: ‘The dragon appears in the field—auspicious to see the great person.’ The Master said: ‘Dragon virtue, centered and correct.’

People fail to grasp the dragon’s life-generating power and are often harmed by it. If one awakens, fears it, regulates and subdues it, one can then drive and employ it. Raising the east to meet the west is the harmonious union of propriety. *Dui* and *gen* each number eight, flowing *wu* to join *ji*. *Hun* and *po* restrain each other, metal and water do not separate. The two *kan* unite their essence, *qian* and *kun* form the body, and the Dao of the *Yi* does not topple—this must be the balance of two eights to make one *jin*.

The Perfect Yang Master, Yu Yan, said: ‘The ancient *Fire Records* of six hundred chapters merely expand upon the sixty-four hexagrams of the *Yi* to elucidate the full ten-month fire times. The recumbent-moon crucible is the lead furnace, its position in *kan*, where the White Tiger resides. The flowing-pearl palace is the mercury crucible, its position in *li*, where the Green Dragon resides. The White Tiger as the pivot for refinement means the White Tiger guards the cinnabar field, and fire issues from below the navel. The Green Dragon joins it by being driven down to meet the White Tiger. East and west are *kan* and *li*; *hun* and *po* are the sun and moon. The origins of dragon and tiger and the sources of lead and mercury are not two paths. If the adept knows the subtlety of driving the dragon to meet the tiger, then one understands the method of casting mercury into lead.

The elixir method is utterly simple and easy. If one can empty the heart, still the self, concentrate the spirit, and enter the qi cavity, then east and west naturally pair, dragon and tiger mate, and *hun* and *po* unite to produce the purple gold—what need is there for exertion?

When the upper *kan* is in effect, the *dui* hexagram governs, and the moon’s light is half-born—thus its number is eight. When the lower *kan* is in effect, the *gen* hexagram governs, and the moon’s essence is half-formed—thus its number is also eight. Observing the union of the two *kan*, the *qian* and *kun* crucible is established, and medicine, ingredients, and fire times are all contained within. Two eights make sixteen *liang*, one *jin*—the sixty-four hexagrams of the *Yi* correspond exactly to this number, which also symbolizes the subtlety of the elixir Way: yin and yang in perfect balance and union.

When metal enters fierce fire, its color does not fade, and its radiance shines forth. Since the beginning of creation, the sun and moon have never waned in brightness, and true gold has never lost its weight. The sun and moon retain their forms as ever, for gold is born from the moon. At the new moon, the sun bestows its tally, and gold returns to its mother. At the dark moon, they embrace, concealing their outlines, sinking into the cavernous void. Gold regains its original nature, and the crucible’s radiance glows.

The True Unity Master, Peng Xiao, said: ‘The five phases overcome one another—fire overcomes metal, yet when metal meets fire, it becomes a vessel, neither harmed. Thus, the metal embryo in the crucible does not dissipate; its color grows ever more luminous. Since the establishment of the *qian* and *kun* crucible, the sun and moon have infused their essence within, mutually benefiting and growing ever brighter. The gold’s weight remains as before, and the sun and moon perpetually encircle and illuminate. Gold is born from the moon because gold is yin essence, lodged in the west—thus it is said that gold comes from the moon. The moon, from the new moon, receives the sun’s tally and thereby generates gold. When gold returns to its mother, the moon takes charge, and gold reverts to water. At the dark moon, yang qi is exhausted, and the two—gold and water—naturally embrace, concealing their outlines and sinking into the cavernous void. The dark moon symbolizes the year’s end; the new moon, the year’s beginning. When gold and water form within the crucible chamber, they perpetually contain harmonious qi, and success is seen—thus the crucible glows. Glowing means harmony; harmony means gold and water congeal—nature’s Way is complete.’

The Embracing Unity Master, Chen Xianwei, said: ‘The sun, moon, and gold endure the longest. Since heaven and earth opened, the sun and moon have retained their forms without ever waning in brightness, and true gold has kept its weight without ever losing its color—these three are one body. People see only that when gold’s essence flourishes, the moon’s brightness doubles, knowing that gold is born from the moon but not that the moon’s brightness is born from the sun. Thus, at their union, the moon conceals its light, sinking into the cavernous void to receive the sun’s radiance and thereby generate gold. Gold’s nature originally comes from the sun—its hardness, weight, and solidity bear the sun’s color and possess the sun’s nature. All things meet fire and melt, yet when gold enters fire, its color does not fade. Refined a hundred times, it grows harder; tempered in great smelters, it glows redder. Fire is the qi of the Great Yang; gold is the essence of the Great Yin. When gold enters fierce fire, it regains its original nature—thus, when the crucible’s fire blazes, the gold’s color grows ever more vivid, and its radiance glows with loveliness.’

Shangyang Zi, Chen Zhixu, said: ‘This speaks of gold’s function—without gold’s power, the elixir cannot form. Thus, the gold elixir is not the gold or jade of the world, nor that which comes from earth and stone. It is the subtlety of heaven and earth’s creation, the five phases inverted, born from the womb of *qian* and *kun*’s great transformation—this is the true gold.

Today’s blind masters, when they speak of the gold elixir, become flustered, not knowing what it is. They prattle of cultivation yet never hear the name of the gold elixir, nor do they fathom the words of the *Cantong Qi*. They deceive the world. Little do they know that the immortals have clearly pointed out this gold’s divine transformations. There are fools who, upon seeing these texts but failing to discern the true gold’s yin-yang body and function, guess it refers to smelting and furnace fires—what a pity!’”

Alas! If we do not reveal some hint of this to the world, then in ten thousand generations hence, this text will grow ever more lofty and distant. People, unable to glimpse its shores, will abandon it and never read it—how then shall they seek the path of cultivation? Those of superior roots and keen faculties must know: this gold existed before the primal chaos of *hongmeng*, before the division of the Great Ultimate. Originally belonging to *qian*, it is thus called *qian*-gold. When the great kalpa is about to turn, those who would repay the virtue of chaos come to this: as *qian* first joins with *kun*, this gold stumbles and gallops, rushing into the palace of *kun*, and is called *kun*-within-gold. *Kun*, receiving this gold, becomes inwardly replete and transforms into *kan*. The three lines of *kun* were originally all hollow, called *kun*-earth; now, with this gold filling its center, it forms the image of *kan*. *Kan*’s proper position is in the north, the land of *gui*-water. As *kan* is water and gold is concealed within it, it is called water-within-gold. This water-within-gold is a treasure of the prior heavens, yet it cannot long abide in the posterior *kan*. Thus, it transforms into *dui*. *Dui* may leap at the gate of the northern *kan* or occupy the western *you* direction—there, this gold grows day by day, night by night. *You*’s proper position belongs to *dui*, and thus this gold governs the practice of the elixir path within *dui*, hence called *dui*-gold.

Those who refine the elixir must seek the subtle and probe the obscure, tracing beginnings to ends, investigating things to extend knowledge, exploring its source and flow, and examining its roots and sprouts. If one refines the gold elixir, one must seek this gold. To seek this gold, one does not seek in *qian*, nor in *kun*, nor in *kan*, but solely in *dui*. *Dui* as a thing shares the same vessel as *kun*-moon—this is called “same vessel.” It is easy to apply effort to *dui*, difficult to craft with *kun*. *Dui*’s wonder lies in its acting on *kun*’s behalf in the Way. Thus, in refining the gold elixir, apart from this *dui*-gold, all else are side doors that cannot lead to the Dao. The Yellow Emperor and Laozi, the ancient sages and immortals, all used this gold to complete the Dao. King Wen’s *Xun* hexagram, the nine in the fifth place: “First *geng*, three days; after *geng*, three days.” Confucius’ commentary on *Xun* and *Dui*: “The yielding follows the firm.” The noble person, in issuing commands and acting, does so in accord with this. *Geng* is metal. The classic says: “Three days, the moon emerges at *geng*—this is it.” Moreover, Śākyamuni borrowed this gold to become a Buddha, hence called the Golden Immortal. For the gold within *dui* shares the same body as the great yin of heaven, born at the same time as brightness. Thus, the moon in heaven is called the great yin. Because this *dui*-gold shares its function, it is also named the lesser yin, or yin-within-gold. The great yin of heaven receives the radiance of the great yang to complete the seasons. The lesser yin of *dui*’s path continues the great thousand worlds, transforming and giving birth to beings. The immortals, having penetrated the wisdom of former sages, know this gold’s root and source, and trace its wondrous transformations—only this gold’s divine changes are singled out.

That worldly gold can endure as long as heaven and earth, entering fire to grow ever more refined, enduring smelting without losing its weight—how much more so this *dui*-gold, born from the great transformative furnace of *qian* and *kun*? The moon’s light waxes and wanes; *dui*’s gold flows and turns. Thus it is said: “In form, it is like the constant new moon. At dawn, sun and moon form a bi-disc; the moon receives the sun’s tally and manifests a single yang’s light at the *geng-shen* position—this is the great yin of heaven. Correspondingly, this *dui*-gold, in accord with the moon’s new moon, begins to generate the yang elixir at the position of chaos on the third day—this is the lesser yin of the human realm.” Hence it is said: “Gold is born from the moon. At dawn, it receives the tally.” What does it mean for gold to return to its mother? The abode of gold is *dui*; the mother of *dui* is *kun*. *Dui* cannot long retain its gold; the gold, too, acts in due season. *Kun*’s wing is said to “contain pattern and be steadfast, acting in its time.” The sage’s heart is wondrous in this: when this gold is put to use, *dui* returns to its mother and enfolds *kun*, just as the moon at its darkest is enfolded by the sun. Why? At the dark of the moon, at dawn, the moon’s gold body hides its frame, covered by the sun. For one, two, three days, it moves through its degrees, and its radiance returns. Likewise, when gold returns to its mother, the gold’s true essence sinks into profound emptiness, put to the world’s use: one generates two, two generates three, and when the kalpa’s turn comes again, the gold will be reborn.

If this gold is reborn, it must restore its original nature. Why? Nature is *qian*’s function; *qian*’s is the straight. Gold is lodged in *kun*, *kun* in *kan*, *kan* in *dui*. When *dui*-gold unfolds its essence, it restores its original nature, returning this gold to the palace of *qian*. *Qian*’s gold crucible regains its seed, and the refined gold elixir is thus called the “gold fluid returning elixir.” The crucible is called the “awe-inspiring radiance gold crucible”—“awe-inspiring radiance” signifies blazing fire, flourishing and abundant.

Quanzhenzi Yu Yan said: “All things in the world are destroyed by fire, only gold is not. Among the five phases, generation reaches its limit at metal. As a thing, when smelted, it yields to water; when struck, it yields to fire. Its softness resembles wood, its color resembles earth. It embodies all four seasons. Thus, true gold, refined a hundred times, grows ever firmer, never losing its original weight. Since heaven and earth opened, for who knows how many thousands of years, the forms of sun and moon remain constant, never diminishing their brightness. For the essences of yin and yang mutually conceal their abodes, each finding its proper place—thus the forms of sun and moon do not change.” In the elixir method, nothing is more luminously manifest than metal and fire. Metal is the moon; fire is the sun. “Gold is born from the sun; at dawn, it receives the tally”—this is the true yin-gold of the great yin, born in the palace of *kun*, originally transformed by the true fire of the great yang. Its initial reception of qi is like gold: though the moon’s light is born from the sun, the moon receives the sun’s light beginning at dawn. “Gold returns to its mother; the moon at its darkest is enfolded by the sun”—this is gold in the palace of *kun*, guarding fire, just as on the moon’s darkest night, sun and moon hold each other. “Hiding its frame, sinking into profound emptiness”—spirit and qi deeply enter their root, gradually sinking to the sea’s bottom, like the moon’s dark body unseen. “Gold restores its original nature; the awe-inspiring radiance crucible blazes”—the moon’s body is originally black; receiving the sun’s light, it becomes white. Now, enfolded by the sun, hiding its frame, it restores its original blackness. Simply guard its blackness, not asking about its whiteness. Over time, spirit and brightness will come of themselves. In an instant, radiance pierces the crucible; fire’s power blazes intensely. Then, on the third day, *geng* is born at *dui*’s gate. From black silver, refined white silver emerges.

Worldly people, fond of petty arts, do not examine the depth of the Dao. They abandon the correct path to follow deviant byways, seeking speed but blocking progress—like the blind who cannot use a staff, or the deaf who listen to the *shang* note. They drown in water to catch pheasants and hares, climb mountains to seek fish and dragons, plant wheat hoping for millet, or use a compass to draw a square. They exhaust their strength and spirit year after year, yet see no result. If one wishes to know the method of ingesting the elixir, the matter is simple and not complex.

True Unity Master Peng Xiao said: Master Xu observed that worldly people favor petty arts and hasten along swift paths, not knowing that petty arts and swift paths have a beginning but no end. Those who expend great effort achieve little success—like the blind and deaf who, in matters of seeing and hearing, or hunters and fishers who err amid rivers and mountains. Since their choices are misguided and their judgments confused, how can they diligently seek the supreme Way, which is simple and not complex? Moreover, the Golden Liquor Returned Elixir is the supreme Way of ascending to heaven in broad daylight. If one encounters an enlightened teacher or receives divine instruction, follows the wondrous formula, and cultivates accordingly, then the principle of ease and simplicity is attained.

Embracing Unity Master Chen Xianwei said: Worldly people abandon the correct path to follow the deviant, indulging in petty arts and exhausting their minds and strength, yet achieve nothing. How could they know the wonder of the great Dao, which is utterly simple and easy, concise and not complex?

High Yang Master Chen Zhixu said: Worldly people favor petty arts, yet petty arts are not the vessel of the Dao—they are narrow and shallow, unworthy of the great Way. The Dao is vast, encompassing heaven and earth; it is deep and boundless as the sea. People, however, cannot comprehend it. First poisoned by blind teachers, their initial words become their master. The correct Way has no chance to be heard, while side doors and arts of *cai-zhan* are preferred. They abandon the correct path to follow deviant byways, ingesting medicines to seek lightness and ascent, desiring speed but blocking progress. Their essence is exhausted, their nature unnurtured—like the blind who cannot use a staff, or borrowing the Way to engage in empty talk, like the deaf who listen to the *shang* note. Why not study the *Cantong Qi* and the five phases without inversion? Why climb mountains to seek fish and dragons, or sit in dry meditation to pursue immortality? Why plant wheat hoping for millet, or strive for effortless attainment while using a compass to draw a square? Such actions exhaust strength and spirit. Without encountering a sagely teacher, they see no result year after year. Those who wish to know the method of ingesting the elixir—ancient immortals’ words are not complex: "Subdue the *qi* without ingesting *qi*; ingest *qi* only after subduing it. Ingesting *qi* does not grant longevity; longevity requires subduing *qi*." These words are the true and wondrous formula, guiding those of the highest rank.

Whole Yang Master Yu Yan said: The great Way of the Golden Elixir is accomplished through the accumulation of essence and the amassing of *qi*, forming the embryo in a moment and establishing the foundation in a hundred days. After one year, one enters the chamber; after three years, refinement and nurturance follow their proper sequence. Alas, scholars do not examine the depth of the Dao or discern whether their teachers are deviant or correct. They seek quick results, favoring petty arts—some know one aspect but neglect another, some grasp the body but lose its function, confined by partial views and self-satisfied. Worse still, they promote heterodox teachings and slander the correct Way, distorting true scriptures to gain the trust of the unlearned, recklessly teaching the deluded and spreading confusion. Such people are many.

Occasionally, there are those of keen intelligence who refuse to humble themselves to seek instruction, instead poring over old texts in hopes of enlightenment—how is this different from the blind who do not use a staff? As for the ignorant and dull, who do not comprehend the supreme principle but force their conjectures to align with alchemical texts—how is this different from the deaf who listen to *gong* and *shang*?

As for taking the navel as the Mysterious Pass—this is like hunting pheasants and hares by entering water. Taking the two eyes as the Flowery Pond—this is like seeking fish and dragons by climbing mountains. Other practices, such as learning bedroom arts in hopes of immortality or sitting in stubborn emptiness to pursue longevity—are these not like planting wheat yet expecting to harvest millet, or using a compass to seek a square? All these waste effort and energy, leaving one white-haired and bewildered, with no results to show. Alas!

The Golden Elixir is born within *Kan* (Water), forced out by fire to shift position, traversing the Three Palaces before descending into the mouth—hence it is called "ingestion." The essential method is not complex; the oral instructions are most simple. Using gold as the embankment, water enters and flows freely. The gold is reckoned at fifteen, and the water’s measure is the same. When tending the furnace, fix the weights: if five parts of water are in excess, two parts are taken as true. The gold remains as heavy as its original state, while the third part does not enter the fire but accompanies the two. Once the Three Substances are united in proper measure, their transformations are as if divine. Below, the *qi* of the Great Yang lies concealed, steaming and warming. In an instant, it first liquefies, then congeals—this is called the Yellow Chariot.

When years and months draw to an end, nature is destroyed, lifespan harmed, and the body reduced to ashes and dust, resembling dust on a bright window. True Unity Master Peng Xiao says: The Gold Mother resides in the Central Palace as quicksilver. The embankment allows gold and water to flow freely, their natures intertwined. Gold and water follow the celestial stems, each receiving half of the *qi*, together making up a full catty. Once the Golden Sand is produced, the mother is not diminished—hence it is said, "the gold remains as heavy as its original state." The third part that does not enter is true earth. Gold, fire, and wood are the Three Substances; water and fire follow the celestial stems, entering the vessel together, where the three natures unite and the two flavors constrain each other, transforming as if divine.

The Gold Mother, initially steamed by the essence-*qi* of the Great Yang, can then liquefy and congeal—this is called the Yellow Chariot. When the cycle of the stars is complete, the work of yin-yang and the Five Phases is fulfilled, and all forms retreat, their merit returned to the Central Palace—the virtue of the Yellow Emperor’s earth. Thus, it is said: nature is destroyed, lifespan harmed, and one returns to earth’s virtue, where spirit and form become like dust on a bright window.

Embracing Unity Master Chen Xianwei says: To refine the Great Elixir, first use pure gold to build the city walls, encircling them completely. Then take true water and let it enter—only then will there be no leakage. Whether called the gold embankment or the city walls, the meaning is the same. Yet in building the gold embankment, if one understands the principle that the Four Images and Five Phases all rely on earth, then gold will naturally form. The embankment employs the true earth of the Five Phases, which can complete the true gold of the Five Phases—for earth is the mother of gold. Once the true gold of the Five Phases is formed, it can contain the true water of the Five Phases—for water is the child of gold. When water, earth, and gold intertwine, they form a square shape, and the Infant appears within.

When the work ascends, golden light fills the chamber, billowing like a chariot in motion—hence it is called the Yellow Chariot. Yet when tending the furnace, the gold’s weight should not exceed five parts. If the water is slightly more, it is no hindrance. The third part that does not enter the fire, accompanying the two, refers to wood (three) and fire (two). Fire (two) and wood (three) do not enter, just as a person’s hun and shen are originally formless, manifesting through things. In the work of self-cultivation, one refines water, earth, and gold. Once these Three Substances are united and the treasure formed, the hun and shen naturally accompany it.

Water entering the gold embankment is originally congealed liquid, steamed and refined by the *qi* of the Great Yang below, transforming into the Yellow Chariot. When the fire’s power is complete and the divine work fulfilled, a thousand changes and ten thousand transformations arise—phoenix carriages and dragon chariots are all of this substance. When the embryo is shed, the body shimmers like sunlight casting dust on a bright window—this is the manifestation of Master Xu’s accomplished transformations. Alas, how can those who do not know, recklessly speculating without ever dreaming of it, dare to fabricate theories? Only those who have personally experienced it can understand.

Upper Yang Master Chen Zhixu says: These words describe entering the chamber, tending the furnace, beginning the work, and sealing the elixir within the crucible. Those of the highest capacity should clearly understand this text, which is most orderly and not at all vague. This section contains the essentials—without this one section’s details, how could later generations begin the work of elixir refinement? Those who practice elixir cultivation but have not met a teacher will find this text profound yet obscure. Upon reaching this section, they will be like chewing wax, with no entry point, and can only guess it refers to smelting the Five Metals and Eight Stones. In the end, they achieve nothing and blame the sagely masters for idle talk—truly pitiable.

Now, to dispel doubts forever: "Using gold as the embankment" refers to the great cultivator who, in refining the Nine-Return Golden Elixir, must understand that this gold is the gold within *Dui* (Lake) of the West. First, prepare the true heart to seek that *Dui* gold, establish an altar, and constantly maintain vigilance. Fortify the embankment to await the birth of this gold’s water. The water thus born must be carefully examined and discerned: is this water of the Prior Heaven or the Posterior Heaven? If it is of the Posterior Heaven, the water is turbid and cannot be used to refine the Returning Elixir. If it is water of the Prior Heaven, one must wait until the water is clear before using it.

A poem says:
*The Jing is muddied by the Wei—*
*For the Jing is clear while the Wei is turbid.*

The elixir cultivator waits for the Jing’s clarity, flowing freely within the embankment, undisturbed—this is what is meant by "water enters and flows freely." Within this clear water lies true gold. Zhou Xingsi says: "Gold is born in the Li River, clear to the utmost." Moreover, one must know its weight and measure before using it. This *Dui* gold must be precisely fifteen taels, approximating one catty—hence it is said, "the gold is reckoned at fifteen." When the gold weighs fifteen taels, it can generate the Li River’s water.

What is meant by "the water’s measure is the same"? It does not mean the water is also fifteen taels, but that the water corresponds to the gold. For fifteen taels of gold, there is a certain amount of water it can generate—hence it is said, "the same." Thus, Master Xu repeatedly emphasizes: when tending the furnace, first fix the weights. If fifteen taels of gold have generated five parts of water, the water is in excess and cannot be used—hence it is said, "five parts of water are in excess." If this gold initially generates two parts of water, this is truly usable—hence it is said, "two parts are taken as true." This two parts of water must correspond to fifteen taels of gold—hence it is said, "the gold remains as heavy as its original state." If the water has reached three parts, it is also unusable—hence it is said, "the third part does not enter." When the measures of gold and water are timely and equal, swiftly combine them with two parts of fire—hence it is said, "fire (two) accompanies them."

Once gold, water, and fire are united, the fire receives the gold’s *qi* and is further restrained by the water, forming the Returning Elixir, which can then transform as if divine.

Here begins the crucial work of approaching the furnace—nothing is more essential than this. Thus, the sage takes the year to select the month, places gold within the moon, measures the day to heed the tide, chooses the hour within the day to correspond with the hexagram, and fixes the fire within the hour to enact the talisman. What is meant by "enacting the talisman"? The ancient sages and former worthies regarded the refinement of the Golden Elixir as a matter of utmost importance. They calculated the seasons and established the method of accumulation, condensing the seventy-two seasonal nodes of a year into a single day, gathering the three hundred sixty hexagrams of a year into a single month, and dividing the thirty-six talismans across a day and night to mark the twelve hours. Within one hour, there are six nodes—yet in seeking the Elixir, only two nodes are employed. Within one hour, there is one hexagram—yet in seeking the Elixir, not even half a hexagram’s moment is needed. Within one hour, there are three talismans—yet in seeking the Elixir, only one talisman’s span is used. This is what is called the "single talisman, single method." Thus, the Yellow Emperor spoke of the *Yin Fu* (Tally of Yin): this is it. Hence it is said, "People know its divinity, yet the divine knows not why it is divine"—this is the reason.

When the immortal cultivator of the Elixir seizes this single talisman’s span, they compress the three thousand six hundred breaths of primordial *qi*, reversing and drawing them into the womb. At this moment, they seize the creative power of Heaven and Earth, steal the essence of the sun and moon. The earth’s axis takes form in the heart, the celestial gate rests in the hand. They blend the *qi* of the dragon and tiger, pound the true essence of gold and water into one. The serpent coils within the elixir furnace, the crow and hare traverse the Yellow Road. Black and white intermingle, hardness and softness alternate in succession. Auspiciousness is stored in the jade chamber, purple radiance reflects the sun. The fiery star guards the western pole, the Vermilion Bird flames in the void. They hasten the movement of water, urge the entry of metal, and press fire into the crucible. Steaming with the *qi* of the Great Yang, it coalesces into the Elixir of the Yellow Chariot.

When first refining gold and water, one guards against reckoning in years and months. Yet at the moment of combining the Elixir, only a single talisman’s effort is used. If prolonged, it harms one’s nature and damages the Elixir; if even slightly deficient, it shortens one’s lifespan. Thus it is said, "When years and months are nearly spent, nature is harmed and lifespan injured." The cultivation of the Elixir is fundamentally for extending life and ascending to truth—yet if off by a hair’s breadth, it instead harms one’s longevity. Therefore, Master Xu admonished later students: one must be cautious and meticulous. The "dust on the bright window"—this is the Elixir’s subtlest point.

Quanzhenzi Yu Yan said: In the method of the Elixir, first use half a catty of metal as the outer furnace, establishing the embankment in the southeast. Then let half a catty of water descend from the west into the northern inner furnace, so that its force is not constrained but flows freely and naturally. The ascent of metal spans from the first to the fifteenth day—fifteen days in total. The descent of water spans from the sixteenth to the thirtieth day—also fifteen days in total. This is what is meant by "half a catty each of metal and water." However, the method requires that the ascent be civil (wen) and the descent martial (wu). Without this, it cannot deeply reach the nine springs below. Hence it is said, "when approaching the furnace, fix the weights—five parts of water are in excess."

When metal and water combine to form the weight of one catty in the ratio of two to eight, opening and closing in endless alternation, this is the true yin and yang of our body. Yet the water must be slightly over half a catty, while the metal must not fall short of its half-catty weight. Hence it is said, "two parts are taken as true; the gold remains as heavy as its original state." As for the earth that "does not enter," this is because the crucible’s circumference contains only half a catty of metal above and half a catty of water below—there is no place for earth. Hence it is said, "it does not enter." Yet this is not truly "not entering." Earth has no fixed position; there is nowhere it does not enter. For example, among the twenty-four positions of Heaven and Earth, there is no wu-ji (戊己). Does this truly mean there is no wu-ji? From ren-zi to gui-hai, it wanders without constancy, rising and falling without regularity—there is nowhere that is not the domain of wu-ji. "Two accompanies them": earth pervades the crucible, moving together with the two, metal and water. When metal, water, and earth move as one, the three substances mutually contain and receive, merging the two into one. Merging the two into one, the clouds of ten thousand acres on Green Mountain are stilled, and the moon of one wheel is scooped from the azure pool—its transformations are as if divine.

Now, the ascending is metal, the descending is water, and what enables their ascent and descent is earth. Yet metal, water, and earth are but metaphors. The Great Dao has always been beyond names and forms—how could there be metal, water, or earth? The *Yuzhi Shu* states: "Refine the Elixir with the *qi* of the zi hour, when yang arises and the fire’s power is complete. At other times, the fire is not so." For at the zi hour, the Great Yang is in the north, and in the human body, it reaches the Gate of the Tailbone. Kindling the fire at this time unites inner and outer, allowing one to steal the mechanism of Heaven and Earth to form the Elixir. Initially, the Great Yang is below, water and fire mate, and the two *qi* steam and blend into liquid. Next, the fire within water ignites, yang *qi* gradually blazes, and the liquid congeals within, pressing out the golden radiance—this is true lead. As it is employed and ascends, it surges like a chariot traveling the Yellow Road, hence called the "Yellow Chariot."

When the work deepens and the fire’s timing completes a celestial cycle, it is like the thirtieth day of the twelfth lunar month, when Heaven’s movement is about to conclude. Then the true nature hides, and lifespan also comes to an end. This is what is meant by "shortening lifespan without duality—cultivate the body and await it."

People merely know that at the zi hour, when kidney *qi* arises, firing and refining can congeal it into liquid, mistaking this for true lead to be taken and transformed into the true mercury of the Li Palace. Yet they do not consider: once it has become liquid, it has form, substance, weight, and turbidity—how could it flow upward against the current? When immortals make the Elixir at this time, they merely kindle fire below to stir its *qi*. When the fire’s power is strong, the *qi* naturally billows upward, like clouds rising over mountains and rivers. Only after ascending into the Mud Pill Palace does it transform into sweet dew and descend into the Double Towers—never once using its substance. The Elixir method speaks of "taking the clear and discarding the turbid." The turbid sinks down—this is the form and body, becoming ash and earth. The clear floats up—this is like the dust on a bright window.

The *Cuixu Pian* says: "Hasten to return the hundred vessels to their source; when the pulse halts and *qi* ceases, the Elixir begins to form." An ancient song says: "Lead is the mother of the sprout, the sprout is the child of lead. Once the golden radiance is obtained, abandon lead and do not use it." It also says: "When it comes time to use lead, using lead is still a mistake"—its caution is profound.

Peng Haogu appended: This speaks of the Earthly Prime’s work. The Earthly Prime’s initial steps rely entirely on the three substances: metal, water, and fire. Within blackness, take white. Use metal as the embankment for water, so that metal and water flow freely, their natures in harmony. Calculating their weights: metal’s fifteen units correspond to the first to fifteenth days, totaling half a catty of metal above. Water’s fifteen units correspond to the sixteenth to thirtieth days, totaling half a catty of water below. As for the gathering, it lies in approaching the furnace and weighing the taels. Twenty-four zhu make one tael, one hundred ninety-two zhu make eight taels. Two zhu and four lei make one qian; one zhu and two lei make five fen. Water weighing five fen does not exceed one zhu and two lei—this is no concern. Yet at this point, it is already in excess, and the metal, from beginning to end, remains only eight taels, unable to balance with the water.

The Heavenly One generates water, the Earthly Four generates metal. In refining the Golden Elixir, only these two are true. The Heavenly Three’s wood does not enter into it, while the Earthly Two’s fire is the primordial fire within the Great Yang, which ever accompanies metal and water and cannot be separated from them.

Why is this so? The elixir is but metal and fire. The medicine is the parent of fire, and fire is the offspring of the medicine. Water resides within metal—thus they form the Three: metal, water, and fire. Once these three unite according to the proper method, the hun and shen naturally undergo wondrous transformations without end.

At first, the Great Yang lies below, its essence and qi steaming and brewing, gradually congealing the metal fluid. Next, fire arises within water, the yang qi blazing, and the metal fluid slowly solidifies. Later, when the fire’s power is sufficient, the metal fluid congeals completely and gathers in the Central Palace, becoming the divine chamber that gives birth to the numinous mercury, called the Yellow Chariot.

When the forging and refining have deepened and the years and months are nearly complete, the three substances all perish, their natures damaged and their years spent. The form and body transform into ashes and dust, glowing and flickering like sunlight through a window or motes of flying dust—intangible and beyond grasp.

These two are considered true, while the third does not enter. Ancient and modern interpretations differ: some take the two as the two phases of the medicine, with the third as the three phases, and beyond the four phases lies another wondrous use not included within the three phases. Others take the two as the two yang months, when the metal emerges from the geng direction and is suitable for gathering, while the third is the three yang months, when the metal is at its fullest and too distant for medicine-gathering. Still others take the two as half a catty of metal and half a catty of water, with one tael of lead containing three parts of divine water and one tael of cinnabar containing three parts of divine fire—this formless medicine is not included in the weight of the metal exchanged.

Upon careful reflection, none of these interpretations is entirely satisfactory. Those who grasp the principle must discern it for themselves.

In pounding, refining, and combining, hold fast as you enter the Red Gate. Secure its borders and defenses, ensuring they are complete and firm. Kindle the blazing fire below, maintaining its sound day and night with diligent care. Begin with the civil and end with the martial. Observe the signs, exercise caution, and carefully regulate the cold and warmth, cycling through the twelve nodes. When the cycle is complete, renew the effort, drawing close to the qi until life’s breath is nearly spent and death approaches. The hun and po transform, and the color shifts to a radiant purple—thus is the Returned Elixir formed. Powdered and shaped into a single pill the size of a knife’s tip, it is most divine.

Master True One Peng Xiao says: Pound and refine the foundation of the elixir until it is firm and complete, then secure the crucible within, calling it the Red Gate. Above, water flows downward; below, fire blazes upward. From new moon to full, advance and retreat; day and night, ascend and descend. The civil fire arises at midnight, the martial follows at dawn, ceasing at noon and beginning again with the yin tally until midnight. Govern the waxing and waning, adjusting the cold and warmth through the twelve nodes. When the cycle ends, begin anew. When the fire is sufficient, the hun and po change form, transforming into radiant purple gold—the Elixir is complete. Ingesting a single grain the size of a knife’s tip brings wondrous and boundless merit.

Master Embracing Unity Chen Xianwei says: This speaks of the work of activation, moving the bellows of Heaven and Earth. Pound and refine until reaching the southern Red Gate, then firmly seal it so that water and fire meet at their borders. This work continues day and night without cease. First ascend with the civil, then descend with the martial, cycling through the twelve hours. When the day ends, renew the effort, drawing close until the qi is nearly exhausted and life’s breath is on the verge of extinction. The hundred vessels return to their root, the ten thousand apertures fall silent—this is not death, yet it resembles death. After extinction, revival comes: the golden light turns purple, taking the form of purple powder. A mere knife’s tip of it appears here and there, its transformations unfathomable, its divine wonders beyond thought.

Master Supreme Yang Chen Zhixu says: Pounding and refining are the intermingling of yin and yang. Holding fast means preserving and gathering it in. The Red Gate is the door of qian; the elixir returns through qian’s door to the divine chamber. Securing it means closing the breath; the defenses are the nine apertures, all of which must be firm and complete, without loss. The blazing fire below, maintained day and night with diligent care—this is because when the yang elixir first arrives, it bears the signal of the fire within li. Day and night, it circulates through the body, and the hundred nodes and ten thousand spirits all obey its command. One must guard it diligently, keeping the sound still and the intent harmonious, the breath even and the pulse settled, so the elixir may begin to congeal.

"Begin with the civil and end with the martial" means that at the start of elixir-refining, one uses the civil fire, while the beginning and end both employ the martial fire. At the start, the martial fire refines the self; at the end, it warms and nurtures. Thus, the three phases are said to be martial at the beginning and end, civil in the middle.

"Observe the signs and exercise caution" means one must not be careless. As the Mud Pill Palace says, "If the work is insufficient, it will not be square and round." "Carefully regulate the cold and warmth" means not to be deceived by people or things. As the Purple Yang Elder said, "Adjust the fire’s timing, entrusting it to yin and yang."

Cycling through the twelve nodes, beginning anew each time, continue until the mercury is replenished and the lead is drawn out. When the lead is nearly exhausted and the mercury dries, the seven po die and the hun transforms—this is the qi being spent, life’s breath nearly gone, the hun and po on the verge of death.

At this stage, the color shifts to radiant purple gold—the Returned Elixir of cinnabar. "Powdered and shaped into a single pill the size of a knife’s tip, most divine" means its smallness is like a pinch of powder, like a grain of millet called a pill. Its lightness is like the tip of a knife—utterly minute. Yet its divine wonders are beyond description.

This passage thoroughly describes the work of beginning the practice. Yet its subtleties and mysteries must be transmitted orally by a master—who could rely on the text alone to accomplish the task?

Master Quanyang, Yu Yan, states: The great elixir of the Golden Pill is born from the Kun earth, yet its seed lies in the Qian heaven. Qian resides above as the crucible, Kun below as the furnace. Without fierce firing and extreme forging, it cannot emerge from the furnace; without counterflow and reverse rotation, it cannot ascend to the crucible. The grinding, refining, and merging—these two are captured from their respective places and brought together in a single furnace, where a single ladle of divine water congeals into true butter.

When entering the Crimson Gate, one seizes the essence and marrow of the hare and crow, which must be swiftly gathered into the crucible and fired. The *Dacheng Ji* says: "Carry it to the crown and bind the Three Flowers, fasten the Golden Gate and Jade Lock." When golden cinnabar ascends to the crucible, the sealing must be firm and meticulous, so that the sacred embryo may be complete and unyielding.

This is the work of beginning in the postnatal realm. Within it, there is also the movement of spiritual fire to observe the true heart, and the stirring of the Xun wind to draw in the true spirit—subtle functions unknown to most. The *Jianwu Ji* says: "Because the fire of the elixir burns below, the Yellow River’s waters flow backward." Thus, the fire of refinement must burn intensely. When the fire in the Cinnabar Field blazes, clouds steam and mists surge; wind stirs in the Mud Pill Palace, and the roars of dragons and tigers resound.

At the time of gathering the medicine, concentrate the spirit and gather the qi, with breath flowing continuously without interruption. Over time, the spirit settles and the qi stabilizes, naturally causing the Xun Gate to thunder, dragons to soar, and tigers to leap, driving the tail back to the empty cavity, chasing the flame into the Celestial Thoroughfare, and rushing upward to the King’s Palace. The *Baoyi Yun* says: "Civil fire gives rise, martial fire solidifies—begin with the civil and end with the martial; one cannot rely on a single path."

In vigilant observation, one must seal the orifices, lower the curtains, and contain the light, silently awaiting the arrival of heaven and earth’s qi. Only then does one stabilize the breath to gather it and assemble the fire to refine it. One must carefully assess its maturity, not acting carelessly. In examining cold and warmth, adjust the fire’s intensity; in examining slowness and urgency, proceed gradually and fiercely, not hastily or abruptly.

The twelve nodes are the twelve celestial stems within the body—positions of the fire’s timing. The fire’s timing ascends from *zi* to *wu* and descends from *wu*, circling the exterior of the crucible. When the entire celestial cycle has been traversed, the celestial net returns to *zi*, hence it is said: "One must be personally attentive."

When the Golden Pill congeals, the Jade Armillary and Jade Balance halt their turning, and the sun’s spirit and moon’s essence both sink into the northern sea’s depths, extinguished and concealed, as if dead. At this moment, one returns to the root and revives the mandate; the spirit congeals and the qi coalesces, the eight vessels all still, breath entirely absent, the qi as if severed. After this severance, there is rebirth—what is called "this time, a great death, now truly alive."

The *Cuixu Pian* says: "Shedding the yellow and donning the purple—what is the reason? Only because the River Chariot has turned deeply." When the nine revolutions of the fire’s timing are complete, the Returned Elixir shines brilliantly, transforming into the radiant light of purple gold. It also says: "Gather it, refine it—before a moment passes, the qi flows ceaselessly through the Three Passes. The Three Passes come and go, the qi endless; a single white meridian ascends to the Mud Pill Palace. Above the Mud Pill Palace is the Purple Gold Crucible; within the crucible, a lump of purple gold transforms into jade nectar, flowing into the mouth, fragrant and sweet, refreshing and cool, filling the tongue. Swallowing it, it enters the five viscera, harmonizing the organs, strengthening the body, and bringing peace. For the Returned Elixir entering the mouth is like honey, sweet and fragrant as the coolness of *polan*—this is the 'knife’s tip, the corner of the jade tablet,' a mere trifle. Yet upon success, its thousand transformations and ten thousand changes are wondrous beyond measure, incomparable to minor arts of side paths. It is rightly called divine."

The numbers of *zi* and *wu* combine to form three; *wu* and *si* are called the Five Threes. When harmonized, the Eight Stones establish the proper order. Breath contains and nurtures, awaiting union as husband and wife. Yellow earth is the father of metal, flowing pearl the child of water. Water takes earth as its ghost; earth restrains water from rising. The Vermilion Bird is the essence of fire, balancing victory and defeat. When water prevails, fire ages; when the old man revives, the aged woman becomes the youthful maiden, reshaping to escape worldly calamity—this is called the True Person, the True Unity.

Master Peng Xiao of the True One says: "The *zi* water is numbered one, the *wu* fire numbered two; together they form three. The *wu* and *si* earth are numbered five. Three and five combine to form eight—this is the harmony of the Three Fives, the proper order of the Eight Stones." Thus, the Green Dragon calls to the White Tiger, and the White Tiger inhales the Green Dragon; breath contains and nurtures, awaiting union as husband and wife.

"Yellow earth is the father of metal, flowing pearl the child of water"—earth can restrain water, so mercury does not fly away; this is the earth phase of the four seasons’ tail fire. Metal is complete through the Vermilion Bird, the spirit of fire, which balances victory and defeat. When water prevails, fire is extinguished; when the new moon and crescent both end, merit returns to earth’s virtue.

When the three natures unite, they return to their original nature and shared ancestor. This means that metal and fire arise from the same number within the water’s qi, for they are born from the primordial qi before heaven and earth, capable of generating the Five Phases—not merely the two flavors of metal and water.

Master Chen Xianwei of the Embracing Unity says: "The Eight Stones are the external medicine. Using the Three Fives as analogy: *zi* water is one, *wu* fire is two; the numbers of *zi* and *wu* combine to form three. Earth is numbered five, hence *wu* and *si* are called five. The harmony of the Three Fives is the union of water, fire, and earth. These three act as husband and wife, alternately as ruler and minister, like the Eight Stones mutually regulating one another. Earth generates metal, so earth is the father of metal; earth restrains water, so water is the ghost of earth. Flowing pearl is mercury, born from the sun and congealing into metal; metal generates water, so flowing pearl is the mother of water. Watering it, fire does not blaze; restraining it with earth, water does not overflow. Thus, the three substances become one family, all returning to *wu* and *si*. Water subdued by earth dissipates; fire subdued by earth is extinguished; metal subdued by earth returns to its father. Earth is the father of metal, so fire is the ancestor of metal—hence, when the three natures unite, the original nature shares a common ancestor."

Master Chen Zhixu of the Upper Yang says: "*Zi* resides in the north, the proper position of *kan*, numbered one; *wu* resides in the south, the proper position of *li*, numbered two. Within *kan* is earth, called *wu*, numbered five; within *li* is earth, called *si*, numbered five. *Wu* guards the gate of *kan*, controlling the qi of the primordial True Unity; *si* directs the door of *li*, accumulating the mercury of the postnatal utmost truth. To seek the primordial qi, one must pass through *wu* earth; to use the postnatal mercury, one must subdue it with *si* earth. When *zi* and *wu* joyfully harmonize, and *wu* and *si* unite, the essence of the two fives congeals and solidifies. *Wu* earth enters the *si* crucible, where the two earths bind—hence the name *gui*. The Eight Stones are Qian and Kun; Kun is the image, the father and mother of stones. Without Kun, one cannot obtain the order of *dui*. *Zi* and *wu* call to each other, *wu* and *si* contain and nurture, lead and mercury intertwine as husband and wife."

Yellow earth is *wu* earth; *wu* earth can generate metal within *dui*, thus it is the father of metal. Flowing pearl is wood-mercury; lead-water can nourish the mercury within wood, thus flowing pearl is the child of water. Lead-water takes *wu* earth as its ghost—once *wu* earth stabilizes the central palace, water does not recklessly flow outward. The Vermilion Bird is the substance within *li*, the essence of fire. When the heart is calm and qi harmonized, the pulse settles, allowing one to regulate its dominance and submission.

Water overcomes fire, fire overcomes metal, metal overcomes wood—these four ultimately dissolve their functions, returning to the fertile earth. Fertile earth is *si* earth. The three natures are *wu* metal and water. The gate of *kan* is called *wu*; the central line of *kan* is *dui* metal. Metal generates the water of Great Unity; once metal generates water, *wu* further restrains it—this is the convergence of the three natures in mutual containment. The wood nature is *si* earth; the door within *li* is called *si*. When *wu* metal, water, and *si* earth unite with the wood nature of *si*, wood is gradually overcome. All transform into the Great Elixir, hence it is said: "The original nature shares a common ancestor."

Master Quanyang, Yu Yan, said: "The number of *zi* water is one, *wu* fire is two; combined they form the number three. The number of earth is five, thus the central *wu* and *si* are called five. Three and five together make eight, hence it is called the Eight Stones. When three and five harmonize, water, fire, and earth unite as one."

Moreover, earth overcomes water, water overcomes fire—how can they harmonize? It is because earth serves as the mediator between water and fire, reconciling and uniting them, enabling water and fire to bind as husband and wife, thus achieving harmony. Once the Eight Stones unite as one, the fundamental principles are rectified, and all phenomena unfold.

Yang ascends, yin descends—heaven and earth breathe within. This is the path to longevity; those who emulate it may also attain longevity. The *Jindan Dacheng Ji* states: "Exhale from the heart and lungs to connect with the celestial root; the dragon’s chant rises like clouds. Inhale into the liver and kidneys to connect with the terrestrial root; the tiger’s roar stirs the wind. Through this breathing, wind and clouds congeal into golden liquid—this is the natural respiration of the primal qi, not the breathing of mouth and nose."

If one can empty the heart, concentrate the spirit, and turn the light inward to illuminate the true person’s breath, following its ascent and descent, then after a short while, breath will mutually nurture, and one will stand in tranquil stillness. Thus, all becomes one, binding as husband and wife.

Liao Chanhui said: "Facing the navel’s wheel, behind the kidneys, at the center lies the true golden crucible—this is its place." Earth dwells at the center, hence it is called yellow earth; earth generates metal, thus it is the father of metal. True mercury flows and moves without fixed form, hence it is called flowing pearl. When it enters water and solidifies into metal, metal generates water, thus it is the mother of water. Now, earth enters water, and water is restrained by earth, unable to carry metal upward—hence it is said: "Water takes earth as its ghost." Earth fills water, preventing it from rising.

The Vermilion Bird is the fire essence of the southern direction, governing the summer season. Now, *kan* water is being subdued by earth; if it encounters the fierce firing of the southern fire, the fire will blaze intensely, the water will boil, and the metal will ascend with the water. Thus it is said: "The Vermilion Bird is the fire essence, balancing and regulating dominance and submission." When the boiling water surges upward into the *li* palace, *li* fire is in turn overcome by *kan* water. Fire, being overcome by water, dissipates—yet water must not overflow. Thus, earth is again used to restrain water, and water is stabilized by earth. Hence it is said: "Water and fire both return to earth."

When water and fire encounter earth, they become the three natures. Once the three natures unite, they merge into one, all returning to the *kun* palace—hence it is said: "The three natures share a common ancestor." Sesame can prolong life; the returning elixir can be ingested. Metal’s nature does not decay, thus it is the treasure of all things. Alchemists who consume it attain long life. Earth travels through the four seasons, guarding boundaries and establishing rules. Golden sand enters the five viscera, its mist and vapor like wind and rain, steaming and reaching the four limbs. The complexion becomes radiant, white hair turns black, fallen teeth regrow in their original sockets, old men regain youth, and aged women become maidens. The form is transformed, worldly calamities are averted—this is called a true person.

Master Zhenyi, Peng Xiao, said: "Giant sesame is sesame. Even those who consume it can prolong life—how much more so the golden liquid returning elixir? Once ingested, can one not attain immortality? The returning elixir first arises from true gold; the gold body is indestructible. This true gold is the ancestor of heaven and earth’s primal qi, the mother of all things. The *Daodejing* states: 'Nameless, it is the beginning of heaven and earth; named, it is the mother of the myriad things.' Before heaven and earth, the primal qi was the origin, giving birth to all phenomena. Gold is the root of water, taken as the foundation of the medicine—thus true gold, the mother, can produce golden sand and form the returning elixir."

Earth travels through the four seasons, marking the beginning and end of the elixir path. Master Xu admonished later generations: the refinement and consumption of this medicine are wondrously unlike ordinary drugs. When this elixir enters the mouth, it is like clouds, mist, wind, and rain, directly entering the five viscera and four limbs, restoring youth, reversing aging, regenerating hair, and regrowing teeth—granting long life and enduring vision.

Master Baoyi, Chen Xianwei, said: "Sesame is also called giant sesame—this is an ordinary medicine. Even consuming it can prolong life; how much more so the divine elixir, the pure yang essence, whose nature is indestructible like vajra? Gold is the most precious treasure among all things. If one obtains and consumes it, longevity is assured—how could it not be ten thousand times superior to ordinary medicine?"

The four directions—*chen*, *xu*, *chou*, and *wei*—all contain earth, demonstrating that metal, wood, water, and fire all rely on earth to stand. Though the five viscera correspond to metal, wood, water, and fire, in truth, they rely on the five earths to flourish. Metal is the child of earth. When the true elixir enters the abdomen and the qi of metal penetrates the five viscera, a misty vapor pervades the body, steaming like a kiln when the fire is blazing, with water rising and descending like smoke and mist. At that time, the four limbs and hundred vessels are suffused as if by spring rain, steaming and flowing naturally. The complexion is renewed, bones are transformed, old age returns to infancy, the countenance becomes radiant, the spirit joyful, white hair turns black, fallen teeth regrow, old men become youthful, aged women become maidens, the form is altered, and worldly calamities are escaped. Day and night, clarity prevails; the spirit remains undimmed. The dharma body and illusory form are both fulfilled; yin spirit and yang spirit are equally wondrous—only then can one be called a true person.

At that time, though mingling with sages and mortals, one transcends the three realms. Though dwelling in the impure world, one’s actions and concealment are unfathomable. If one wishes to depart, one directly reaches Penglai; if one desires to roam freely, one instantly transcends the external world.

Master Shangyang, Chen Zhixu, said: "Giant sesame is sesame. If one regularly consumes it as food, it can prolong life—how much more so the returning elixir, refined from metal, water, *wu*, and *si*, becoming the supreme treasure of heaven and earth? Alchemists who subdue and consume it attain longevity equal to the sun and moon. 'Subdue' means to subdue the primal qi; 'consume' means to swallow the millet-sized elixir. Later generations mistakenly write it as 'serve' (*fu*), unaware of the subtlety of 'subdue' (*fu*)."

Thus, the immortal masters say: "To subdue qi, not to consume qi; to consume qi, one must first subdue qi. Consuming qi alone does not confer longevity—longevity requires subduing qi." The single word "subdue" (*fu*) operates in reverse, transforming the mechanism. Earth wanders through the four seasons; the four seasons are *chen*, *xu*, *chou*, and *wei*. Earth combines with its days of prosperity: in each seasonal month, it reigns for eighteen days, called its "wandering." Only in summer, when fire generates earth, does earth’s virtue prevail, for metal fears fire. Thus, when autumn arrives, belonging to the *shen* month, the ancients held that both water and earth are born in *shen*: earth is generated by summer’s fire, while water arises at the Three Enclosures, restraining fire so that earth may generate metal. Therefore, at the onset of autumn, earth’s virtue first reigns for nine days, generating *geng* metal, and ceases at *xu*, where its nine-day reign is divided.

To guard boundaries and establish norms: in the east, *Di* earth guards the Azure Dragon’s domain; in the west, *Wei* earth regulates the White Tiger’s power; in the south, *Liu* earth measures the gate of *Li* fire; in the north, *Nü* earth stabilizes the door within *Kan*. Thus, the qi of cinnabar and true gold are subdued and returned into the five viscera. When the elixir first arrives, its qi disperses like mist, moistening like rain. The elixir’s qi steams and permeates the four limbs. Once spirit and qi are complete, the complexion becomes radiant, teeth regrow, hair blackens, old age reverts to youth, and withered forms are transformed. One forever escapes the calamities of the mortal world, achieving wondrous unity of form and spirit.

The Purple Radiance True Person said: "To begin refining the elixir, first harmonize the *wu* and *si* earths; only then may one gather metal and water to form the elixir."

Master Quanyang, Yu Yan, said: "Giant sesame is sesame. Consuming it can still prolong life—how much more so the nine-times-cycled Great Returning Elixir of golden liquid, the time when metal’s essence is robust? Stealing the right qi of heaven and earth to congeal the sacred embryo, how could it not confer longevity? Gold’s nature is firm and unyielding, enduring ten thousand years without decay—it is the supreme treasure among the myriad things. Thus, the immortals esteem it highly. They do not call it the elixir of water, fire, earth, or wood but uniquely name it the Golden Elixir."

Earth has no fixed position but circulates between *chen*, *xu*, *chou*, and *wei*. Spring, summer, autumn, and winter are all places where earth wanders. Earth can exhaust water and conceal fire: when guarding water, water does not flow; when guarding fire, fire does not flame. Now, using it to guard *Kun* while gathering the medicine and to guard *Qian* while circulating fire—this is what is meant by "guarding boundaries and establishing norms."

Thus, when golden cinnabar ascends the crucible, it pierces the two kidneys, guides along the spine, passes through the heart meridian, enters the sea of marrow, rushes through the lung’s transport point, traverses the liver, crosses the spleen, and returns to the elixir field. As it ascends, it billows like clouds filling the four directions, whirls like a sudden storm, flashes like waking from a daydream, and disperses like a chronic illness leaving the body. Spirit and qi unite like husband and wife in embrace, bones and flesh harmonize like bathing and rising—these are the true visions.

From this point, day and night, one nurtures it without interruption, allowing the true qi to steam and reach the four limbs. Naturally, the spirit becomes clear, qi becomes invigorated, the complexion glows, white hair turns black, fallen teeth regrow, old men revert to youth, and aged women become maidens. Transforming form and transcending the world, one leaps from the cage, forever escaping the calamities of the dusty realm, becoming one with heaven and earth without end—thus is one called a True Person.

Extrapolating the numbers of the five phases, the method is concise yet not cumbersome. Using water to restrain fire extinguishes its light suddenly; the sun and moon mutually eclipse, always at the new and full moons. When water flourishes, *Kan* encroaches on yang; when fire wanes, *Li* dims the day. Yin and yang consume each other—this is the natural Dao.

True Unity Master, Peng Xiao, said: "The five phases are the qi of emptiness and nothingness, difficult to perceive. Yet if one examines them through the total numbers of heaven and earth, none escape their operation. Within the crucible, the five phases are constrained, yin and yang unite, fire rises as water retreats, water excites fire’s decline. The sun’s essence (*ri hun*) arises at the new moon, the moon’s spirit (*yue po*) ends at dusk. Male and female alternate, cinnabar and mercury generate each other—heaven and earth act naturally, and the elixir’s path becomes clear."

Embracing Unity Master, Chen Xianwei, said: "If one compares the five phases, fire, when meeting water, is suddenly extinguished. Yet the sun and moon are also water and fire—why, at every conjunction, do they not harm each other? Because heaven and earth’s yin and yang interact and consume each other according to fixed numbers. At set times, there is no harm from water flourishing or fire waning. If one can discern this mechanism and steal its use, then the cosmos is in hand, and the myriad transformations are born in the body. Though water and fire are mutually destructive, they unite as husband and wife; though metal and wood are separated, they naturally communicate. Yet none in the world can see or know this—how lamentable!"

Master Shangyang, Chen Zhixu, said: "The numbers of the five phases—metal, wood, water, fire, earth—extend to the numbers of three, five, and one. In refining the Golden Elixir, lead, mercury, silver, cinnabar, and earth are the five phases, matched to yin and yang. Thus, water can extinguish fire because yin can dissolve yang. The sun and moon eclipse only at the new and full moons, where yin and yang, in their waxing and waning, encroach upon each other. If yin and yang harmonize and mutually consume, then the natural Dao of interaction arises."

Master Quanyang, Yu Yan, said: "*The Book of Changes* states: 'Heaven one, earth two; heaven three, earth four; heaven five, earth six; heaven seven, earth eight; heaven nine, earth ten'—these are the generative numbers of the five phases."

Zihua Zi said: "Among the great numbers of heaven and earth, none surpass five, none center upon five. Five is the number of earth, residing in the center. Combined with the north’s water one, it becomes six; with the south’s fire two, it becomes seven; with the east’s wood three, it becomes eight; with the west’s metal four, it becomes nine. The numbers stop at nine, for nine is the extremity of numbers. Speaking of the five numbers—one, two, three, four, six, seven, eight, nine—five is truly the central number. Numbers originally have no ten; that earth becomes ten arises from the north’s one, south’s two, east’s three, and west’s four converging at the center to form ten. Thus, when the center’s five disperses to the four directions, becoming six, seven, eight, and nine, water, fire, wood, and metal all rely on earth to form. If the four directions’ one, two, three, and four return to the center to form ten, then water, fire, wood, and metal all return to their source and are contained within earth.

Alas! The profound! The enlightened reverse and seek it within themselves—then it is utterly simple and not cumbersome."

The *Wuzhen Pian* states: "Two things arise from the child producing the mother." The *Hunyuan Baozhang* says: "The four positions are distinct, yet their use is inverted; the five phases together rise and together return." Both elucidate this principle. The *Huangji Jingshi* states: "The mutual eclipses of the sun and moon are the convergence of numbers." This principle is no different from the mutual restraint of water and fire. Now, if one pours water to douse fire, the fire is overcome by water, and its light is suddenly extinguished. When the Greater Yin obscures the Greater Yang, the Yang is vanquished by Yin, and the sunlight dims by day. Why is this? The mutual exchange and mutual consumption of Yin and Yang are the natural Dao.

Yet the mutual eclipses of the sun and moon always occur between the last and first days of the lunar month. Those who cultivate the elixir, seeking to steal from Heaven and Earth and seize the workings of Creation—can they not pursue this from this very point? "Naming" defines the essence, while "character" expresses the nature. Only when metal returns to its original nature can it be called the Returned Elixir. I dare not speak falsely; I emulate the sages' writings and ancient records. The titles—*Dragon and Tiger*, the Yellow Emperor’s *Golden Flower*, Huainan’s *Autumn Stone*, Yuyang’s *Yellow Sprout*—the worthy can practice them, while the unworthy have no part in them. From ancient times to the present, the Dao follows a single path. In discourse and planning, scholars must exert effort, ponder deeply, and hold fast to the essentials. The words are utterly revealed, bright and clear, never deceiving me.

Zhenyi Zi, Peng Xiao, says: "Metal is essence; water is nature. When metal gives birth to cinnabar, essence returns to nature. Moreover, metal is born from water, and water is the child of metal. The child, in turn, is born from metal, so water returns as the mother of metal—hence the name Returned Elixir. The earlier text speaks of the mother nurturing the child in the womb, the child nestled in the mother’s embrace. Yet Master Xu’s account is hardly deceptive; he borrows the imagery of the *Yijing* and the ancient *Dragon and Tiger Classic* to discuss it, praising the Yellow Emperor, Huainan, Yuyang, and the earlier perfected sages, all of whom practiced and achieved it. From ancient times to the present, the path is one and the same—beyond the reach of the unworthy. Thus, I admonish later generations to ponder deeply and seek the essential words, which are fully revealed, bright and clear, never deceiving us."

Baoyi Zi, Chen Xianwei, says: "This explains why the Returned Elixir is so named. 'Return' refers to essence, while 'elixir' refers to nature. 'Metal returns to its original nature' means that Metal Duke, born of my nature, now returns to meet its mother and reunites with the Maiden, forming the Infant—hence the name Returned Elixir. As the poem by Ziyang says: 'The Metal Duke was originally the Eastern House’s child, sent to the Western Neighbor to lodge and grow. Once recognized, he is called home to nurture and wed the Maiden.' Though names vary across the ages, the Dao remains one."

Shangyang Zi, Chen Zhixu, says: "Metal and water share the name 'essence,' while wood and fire share the character 'nature.' Essence resides in the northwest, nature in the southeast. The southeast is 'self,' the northwest 'other.' The essence of metal and water naturally comes from without to restrain wood and fire. The nature of wood and fire returns within to congeal the Golden Elixir—this is what is meant by 'metal returns to its original nature' and is thus called the Returned Elixir. These two lines are the marrow of the *Cantong Qi*."

"I dare not speak falsely; I emulate the sages' writings." Master Xu received the true transmission of Boyang’s teachings, cultivated according to the method, and achieved the elixir. He then composed this book to instruct later generations. He recounted the Yellow Emperor’s achievement of the elixir, calling it *Golden Flower*; Huainan’s achievement, calling it *Autumn Stone*; Yuyang’s achievement, calling it *Yellow Sprout*. Each, upon ascending, bore a different name—yet all were this Returned Elixir, all were the primordial unified qi, all were the same substance.

Later generations, hearing *Golden Flower*, guessed it to be the five metals; hearing *Yellow Sprout*, guessed it to be the eight minerals; hearing *Autumn Stone*, guessed it to be urine. How could they know that the ancient sages and perfected ones established these names for convenience? The elixir they refined lies nowhere beyond Yin and Yang—is there another path? This Dao can only be diligently practiced by sages. From ancient times to the present, it has been one and the same. The great sages of the Three Teachings must share this substance to apply their efforts. Thus, it is said: "From ancient times to the present, the Dao follows a single path. In discourse and planning, apart from this one way, there is no other method." Later seekers must exert effort, ponder deeply, and seek a teacher’s guidance—then they will know that this book is bright and clear, fully revealed, never deceiving.

Quanyang Zi, Yu Yan, says: The *Fuming Pian* states: "One thing divides into two; what can make two is called the Two—namely, metal and wood. Metal and wood are not two separate entities. If metal is named, then wood is its character; if wood is nature, then metal is essence. In truth, they are one thing. The Metal Duke was originally the Eastern House’s child, sent to the Western Neighbor to lodge and grow—yet this cannot yet be called the Returned Elixir. Only when it is poured into the Eastern Yang’s alchemical furnace, returns home, and meets the Blue Maiden, producing a luminous pearl like the full moon, can it be called the Returned Elixir. Alternatively, when stillness is unmoving and essence returns to nature, it is also called the Returned Elixir—another meaning. The essential secrets of the Returned Elixir are fully revealed here.

The ancient records—*Dragon and Tiger*, the Yellow Emperor’s *Golden Flower*, Huainan’s *Autumn Stone*, Yuyang’s *Yellow Sprout*—are merely metaphorical names to convey meaning. How could the *Cantong Qi*, a single book, be empty fabrication or groundless speculation? It also emulates the subtle intent of the ancients.
